thinke contrary though ſhe empreſſe fynde emperour huſbande yet ſhe wyll fynde ſome man ſoo determyned wyll change robe ſylke gowne clothe dare well ſaye deſyre yonge ſheparde olde emperour care chyldren ye muſte leaue behind tell ſhuld ſo deth diſpleaſant moch diſpleaſeth yt liue ſo longe great pein child deſire deth father poore feare ſhuld mainteined ryche thā bicauſe ſhalbe heire ſynge wepe fere deth wepe bicauſe leaue life doo know yt night cometh dewy mornyng yt cometh bright ſon ye ſon comith derk cloude ageyn cometh faire wether cometh lightnyng thonder clere aire alſo ſay infancy cometh childhode thā cometh youth age ſo laſte cometh deth dethe fearefull hope ſure lyfe sir beleue one thyng beginning meane ende euery man hath certainly ben takē floure fro herbe ben cut grene fro tree ben graffed primetyme ben eaten ſowernes vyne meane fyrſte youthe whan lyfe ſweteſt dethe come knocked gate ye ſhulde haue cauſe ſory nowe walles weake redye falle flowre wythered putrified ſpeare full moſſe canne drawe knyfe ſhethe herein haue deſired worlde neuer knowen worlde lxii yere haue ben priſoner dongeon body whan ſhakles gyues ſhuld taken complayne lorde wold make thou diddeſt eate rome lernyng thou haddeſt athene thy bringyng vp hous lyfe thou haſte wel ſerued dethe thou haſt well counſayled commande commodus ſonne rewarde thy good ſeruice pray goddis trauaylle dethe weightieſt perillous moſte perillous al ben great gretteſt al thingis haue ende laſt deth ſaufe deth whoſe ende vnknowē hurte deth yt ſicke ſleping euill hauing quicke vnderſtandyng yet knoweth man many thinges beinge offered hym determine vpon none yet againe ſay true faithfull frende ſuch time wil giue good coū ſel frend ſay wyl ſay true ſweare noo man knowe perfitely caſe redye dye lxii yere hath ben cours lyfe nowe deathe commaundeth cloſe myn eies folowe cours deth moreouer thou knoweſt infirmitie ſo thou approcheſt cure helthe dolour thou haſt made defenſiues remembre though ſhe thyn owne mother yet ſhe wyfe peyne curſyng ſuffre ſhe yl intreted domage ſhe ſhuld ſuffre thy cōſent ſhuld gyue euidence ſmal thought thou takeſt deth ſhulde iniury thy life haue kynges natural inhabitauntes citeſens rome dwel within walles rome may ſeruice thou mayſt thē good son intrete ſuche wiſe though good father deade yet let haue fauour though ſe brother emperour rome yet let thē defouled womē ryght tender cōdition wyll complayne ſmalle cauſe leſſe wylle ryſe vp pride thou oughteſt conſerue theym deth haue done lyfe otherwiſe conuerſation ſhulde fekyll people importunate alſo cōmit lipula thy ſiſter amōge virgin veſtales thinke ſhe doughter thy mother fauſtin whiche haue greatly loued lyfe vnto houre death haue lamented euery yere gaue thy ſiſter iim ſexters neceſſities ſhe ben well maried yf ſhe brent vyſage whiche eſtemed euery man yl aduenture ſpecially moder wept alway eſteme yll aduenture good fortune ſhe ben brent face fire ſhe worlde touchyng renome brent diuers tonges son ſwere ſeruice goddes fame men ſhe ſurer virgin temple though ſhe ſenate ſenatours deme ende iourney ſhe ſhal finde ſelf better eaſe cloſed locked thou thy libertie prouynce lucany haue lefte iim ſexters wyll thou take fro alſo cōmytte druſia wyddowe hath layd great proces againſt ſenate bycauſe yt motion afore paſſed huſbande baniſhed haue great compaſſion thre monthes ſythe ſhe put demande bycauſe great warres coude declare iuſtyce sonne thou ſhalte fynde trewe xxxv yere haue gouerned rome neuer wydow helde proceſſe paſſynge viii dayes take compaſſion ſuche womennes neceſſities right peryllous laſte yf beſynes longe hande recouer ſo moche theyr goodes leſe renowme alſo haue compaſſyon poore men goddis ſhall rewarde great ryches alſo commytte auncient ſeruantes longe yeres cruel warres often neceſſities diſpleaſure bodye longe ſyckeneſſes hath ben right paynefull true ſeruantes gyue lyfe haue taken peyn vnto deth reaſon ſyth haue vngentylnes the▪ thou haſt foūde xviii yeres armes abrode halſe ſhulde finde one day thy gate ſhet ageinſt theſe thinges cōmit particularly kepe alway memory ſith remembre deth cōſider loued life doo gyue vnto table counſayles lette laſte worde empyre thou ſhalt feared table thou ſhalte beloued ſayd table delyuered ſonne emperour turned eyen within quarter houre yelded ſpirite ¶nowe retourne ſayd table writing written betwene bulle kynge ſcrowe greke letter maner heroicall verſes conteynynge vulgar tonge thus neuer choſe ryche tirant abhorred poore iuſt man neuer denyed iuſtice poore man pouertie pardoned ryche man great goodes rycheſſe neuer dyd good deedes neuer gaue hyre affection gaue correction onely peyne neuer left ylnes vnchaſtiſed goodnes without reward neuer commytted doo proſperitie diſpayred myne aduerſitie neuer committed yl malic enor villany auarice neuer opened gate flatterars dyſſemblers lyſtened myne eares murmurer haue laboured always loued good dread fered yll fynally haue fauoured poore myght lyttell haue fauored goddis may moche ¶hytherto ſhewed brefely worthy laudable lyfe emperour marcus aurelius deathe hereafter enſueth ſeconde parte boke ¶a letter ſente marcus aurelius pyramon ſpciall frende capitu xlix ¶the fyrſte letter marke oratour romayn borne mount celio pyramon lyon greatte frende deſiringe ſalutation thy perſon ſtrength vertu againſt thy ſiniſter fortune thyrde kalendes ianuarie receiued thy letter wherby perceyue thou haſt receiued one myn ſet ſmall ſtore thy wordes eſteme greatly thou meaneſt without declarynge therof haue gadred ſentence reaſon wolde bycauſe haue written ſo often thou ſhuldeſt better vnderſtande thou arte ſo ſlouthfull though call thou wylt thoughe ſtryke thou wylte feele nowe comme purpoſe thou knoweſt well piramon howe nere parentage auncient frendeſhyppe ſtedfaſte loue tender harte whan ſo euer thou putte experyence one true frende ſhall proue thou remembreſt wel rodes dwelled togyther one houſe dyd eate one table thou thoughteſt dyd effecte ſayd thou neuer gaynſaydeſt certaynly thou hart thyne entrayles thyne thou myne beinge together hit ſemed one one wyll frende piramon thou writeſt howe thou arte heuy yet thou doeſt ſhewe cauſe thou complayneſt yt thou art almoſt deed thou ſheweſt taketh thy life fro thou wilt ſhewe thyn yll deſtenies ſith thou arte frende wyll thou knowe demaunde right thou wylte wyl thou knowe ye pitiefull goddes haue determined pleaſures profyte ſhall departe houſe heuines domages ſhall regiſtred perſonne sithe prince al honour tribulation yf thou woldeſte thou canſte eſcape ſeignourie thou complayne thou arte vnhappy fortune eſteme ſelfe happy vnhappynes demand one thynge whan haſte thou ſene haue ſufficiente thou nede whan haſte thou ſene ſlepe thou wake whan haſte thou trauayled reſted trouthe ſithe goodes perſones theyr owne propre trauayles yl aduentures always common one thynge thou oughteſt knowe myne amitie thou wylte perſeuer goodes thyne thyn euylles myn ſyth thou arte borne lyue eaſyly gentilly ordered intreated lyue trauayle ſay faynyngely thou haſte hadde experience whan iamaria thy ſyſter dyed leſſe vertuous fayre thou ſaweſt wel whan ſhe buried deed buried quick ſowne teares thin eies daunced sythe thou holdeſt ſuche ſureties perſon ſurely thou maiſt diſcouer thy peyne yet often haue demanded hath fayned reaſons fayled require deſyre agayne name goddes pray theyr name coniure thou diſpoſe thy ſorowes myn entrayles way thou goeſte wyll leaue one pace go fro ſame thou go wyll go thou reſte wyll reſte yf thou worke wyll worke thou leue wyll doo ſame thou wylt dye thou knoweſt well wyll lyue regarde frende thou wylt thyne euyls myne tormente bothe one harte thou haue diſpleſure thynges diſpleaſe thou wepe ſwere fro hensforthe neuer laughe thou diſcharge thy peyne fro hensforth ſhall take myne thou go alone wil forſake company forth lyue ſolytarily wylt thou ſhuld deſyre al euer thou wylt wyll thou complayneſt thy trauayles thou canſt fynd parent remedy frend counſel ſwere frende pyramon theſe two thinges haue moche pouertie howſe thou haſt ſorow thyn knowe wel remedy ſhuld come ryches councell conſolation wiſe reaſon heuy deſtenies ſlouthe hath taken fro knowlege wiſedome fortune wyll permytte haue great rich certaynely wepe thy myſerie yet ſmalle remedy thou ſayeſte thy letter thy neyghbours frendes promyſynge haue behighte many thynges giuynge nothyng hereof meruaylle vertuous hand bound make tonge fole truly though fete daunce handes ſhulde werke ſowne tonge lyfe endethe fewe dayes renoume fewer promys aunciēt cuſtome among ſonnes vanite cuſtome tonge ſpeketh haſtily handes worke leyſure nowe lette v ſpeake particularly ¶thou oughteſt complayne thou fyndeſt fewe dyuers haue founde alone cuſtome receyue forthwith meryly gyue ſlowelye ylle wylle repentaunce preſumptuous one whiche ſloutheful grekes ſaye promyſethe longe fulfyllyng ſlacke frende romayns ſay moch better denieth forthwith bycauſe wyll begyle hym aſketh caſe ſay may gyue gyueth clere ennemy promiſeth forthewith longe ſuſpecious frende nede wordis frēdes whā may ſuccour workes right gyue hartis ye beſt thinge within v giue tongue worſte thinge vyces good ſothe goddis wylle ſuffre place amitie deſire thyng frende haſt driuen long delaying plato lawes ſayth commande gouernynge polytike counſayle gyuen proſperitie thentent decay ſuccour heuines trouble thentent deſpaire certainly vnder theſe wordes compriſed dyuers great ſentences thou knoweſt wel frēd piramon ſwete wordes cōfort hart lytle tribulation ſome good workes therwith wyl nat deny haue giuen oure good wylles tyme proſperytie bounde gyue v goodes ſhewe v fauour aduerſitie demande one thing wherfore holdeſt thou preſumptuous lycence demaunde reproueſt part lybertie denieng truly ſhame demanding obligation ſome thyng deny importunate man worthy haue mercy thou mayſt knowe thou knowe frēd piramō attayn euery thing yt demāded belongeth goddis giue al thing demāded ſigne ſeruāt deny thing liberte wepe yt denied cōditiō tirātis conne thanke gyuen condition barbaryens haue euer ſtedfaſte hoope denyed guyſe romaynes one theſe thinges wherein gayus ceſar ſhewed hym ſelfe high courage moſte greatteſt ioye whan ſenate refuſed thynge deſyred hym oftentymes ſayde nothynge wherin rome gyueth glorye renowme perſone thanne whan ſhewe ſelfe moſte haſty demaunde moſte ſtyffe denye thentent ſhuld knowe power abyde howe lyttel theyr ſtrength reſiſt thynk better haue recours goddis vertues diſpleaſe theym quarelles gyue contentation thy repoſed wyll whan thou ſeeſt thy ſelfe tribulation thou demaundeſt goddis men fruſtrate thou oughteſt meaſure ryght meaſure payſe ryght balaunce great quantitie hath bene gyuen lyttell quantitie hath graunted howe vncourteyſe goddis ſmall remembraunce men whan myniſhe forgetfulnes haue receyued lytle hath ben refuſed v augment complayntes frende pyramon begyled thou fyftye yeres age ſeaſon thou haſte done nothyng receyued gyftes yet al haue nat ſeene one day ſeruice certaynly reſon complayne viii dayes yll fortune beynge fyfty yeres age thou ſayeſt thy letter howe thou haſt moch pein bycauſe thou knoweſt thy neyghbours enuyous good ſoth haue peyne thy peyne thy meruaylyng haue great meruayle admiration procedethe ſurmountynge ignorance faulte experience doth quicke vnderſtandynge men rule lyfe thē mortall nede thinke trauayle come hauynge theyr handes haſty remedy hungry maye eate whan colde may warme theym ſlepy maye ſlepe whan wery maye reſt ſycke may healed whan heuye maye reioyce ſuche maner thoughtfull lyfe paſſeth ſome make tiltes lyſtes ſome make armure ſcaffoldes ſome inuente newe gynne ſome repayre bulwarkes ſay world fleſh nought el fyghte ageynſt v haue nede tymes defende v fro theſe remedyes ageynſt trauayle fleſhe ſhall curſednes enuy extende amonge theſe curſed welthe euery man enuieth certaynly agaynſte enuy fortreſſe defend caue hyde hye hil mount thycke wodde ſhadowe ſhyppe ſcape horſe beare away money redeme v enuy ſo venomous ſerpent neuer mortall man amonge mortalles coulde ſcape fro bytynge tothe ſcratchynge nayles foylynge fete poiſonynge poyſon ſwere frende pyramon ſuch fortune lifteth vp great ryches ſhe full crueltie gyueth theym profounde bytynges enuie ſo enuious mooſte denyed ſette fardeſt ſhe gyuethe moſte cruell ſtrokes fete vnhappye enuye prepareth poyſon ſecretely fro reſt among dyuers pleaſures ¶i haue redde dyuers bookes hebrewe greke latyn caldee alſo haue ſpoken many wiſe men ſe might foūde remedy ageinſt enuious man confeſſe truth rede redde imagine al demaunde demaunded ye ſhall fynde none cure ageinſt curſed enuie banyſhe v fro proſperitie ſytte aduerſe fortune howe vnhappy ar proſperitie iuſtely ſette vp hygh eſtate flee perille scilla without fallynge charibdis ſcape peryll without caſtinge treaſures ſee ſay malady enuy wyll ſuffre theym ſcape fro dethe medicine applyed wyll aſſure lyfe determine whiche beſte ſaye properly worſte extreme myſerie without danger fortune extreme proſperitie always thretened falle caſe ſo extreme wyl determin ſith one perillous lyfe renoume ſure ¶i ſhall tell wiſe cicero ſayde whan purſued many rome beholde romaine holde ſo good ſelfe ſo ylle ſaye trouth always always make lye certayne ye bere none enuie ye bycauſe ye caſe rather ennemies enuye proſperitie frendes pouertie ¶this oratour ſpake appetite proſperitie leuynge gyue remedy ſorowfull cicero ſene feldes farſalye toke councell remedy ſuche pleaſed hym rome ceſar granted goodes yet yt turned credence renoume surely frend pyramō know remedy gyue ageinſt enuy ſith thou ſeeſt al world ful therof ſe ſons enuy liue enuy die enuy leueth moſt ryches leaueth greateſt enuy ancient wiſe men coūſailed rich men ſhuld haue pore folkes nere admoniſhed pore ſhuld nat dwell nere rych truly good reaſon richeſſe riche men ſede enuy poore bycauſe pore mā lacketh riche hath moche cauſeth diſcorde among people ſwere ye goddis immortal frēde pyramon though yl wolde ſhuld ſwere falſely moche rich thought noriſheth couetiſe ſo moch enuious noriſheth enuy therby tell one thynge good counſell flee enuy auoyde vertu cō trarye ſame homer ſaithe yt tyme two grekes extreme extremity one extreme rich therfore ꝑſecuted enuy achilles ſore noted malice man enuy hym thieſtes certaynly leuer achilles enuy thā thieſtes without thou knoweſt well romaynes ſerche reſte lyfe honour deathe ſithe ſo poſſible man euery man enuieth renoume ought exalted reſt lyfe ſithe ſee theſe two thynges ſuche thy frendes taketh lyttell thought thyn ennemies murmure ageinſte thou wryteſt howe lyon doo well mery excepte thy ſelfe arte heuy full penſyueneſſe ſith ſhewe haue pleaſure thy diſpleaſure ſhewe thy ſelfe dyſpleaſed pleaſure maye chaunce one day ſhall ſorowfull whan thou art merye thou ſhalt quite euyll perſone greatter yll good man greatter faute diſpleaſed man welthe take pleaſure man harme caſe al v domage enuy yet moche frende enemy myn enmy wyl beware feare wyll withdrawe frende amitie may begyle fidelitie ſhal perceyue amonge mortall ennemies none wors frend enuyous felicitie pyramon frende wylle conclude thou wylt withdrawe thy ſelfe fro ennemies kepe company thyn owne familiar frendes wote write harte lamente thy heuyneſſe thou knoweſt howe thy nyece bruſia ſlayne dagger owne huſbande great compaſſion deth renoume ſhe lefte behynde flauius priſcus thyn vncle newely made cenſure proceſſe betwene thy brother fornion britio determyned ſenate hit pleaſeth ryghte well frendes euerye man well content boke intytuled conſolation heuynes haue ended layde capitol haue writen greke cauſe ſent ſende ryche ſwerde fayre gyrdell fauſtine wyfe dothe ſalute ſendethe thy wyfe two ſclaues goddis kepers comfort thy preſent heuyneſſe marke man fortunate pyramon ſore diſcomforted ¶a letter ſent marcus emperour cornelius trauayle warre vanitie triumph ¶the ſeconde letter marcke emperour rome cornelius faythfulle frende ſalutation thy perſon good fortune thy deſired lyfe thou tyme paſſed haſte bene partener trauayles haue ſente calle gyue pleaſure tryumphes haboundance rycheſſe diuerſitie captiues fierſnes capitayns haue brought rome thou mayſt perceyue peryls haue ſuffred warre parthes good men warre euery man findeth lande defendeth houſes ſtronge hart ſurely lyke good men without reaſon dye affection take men goodes reaſon labour defende owne lette man take enuy romayn capitayn triumph gyuen mother rome one day honour dayes diſpaire lyfe wylle ſpeake myght ſay warre dwell rome ben cruell iuges owne fame ſith ꝓpre renome man lyeth folkes tonges ſayde bycauſe perſone hath meryted bycauſe doo ſhewe theyr enuye foolyſhenes ſo folyſhe reputation men ſoo vayne one vayne worde profytte put lyfe daunger lay honour gauge trauayle rather lyue aſſure renoume reſte ſwere goddis immortall daye tryumph chariot penſiue myght rome curſed thy foly wo hym hath brought vp ſoo moche pride curſed hath inuented ſo great pompe greatter vnegall lyghtnes romayne capitayn bicauſe hath conquered realmes altered peaſibles dyſtroyed cityes caſte downe fortreſſes robbed poore enriched tyrantis ſhedde moche bloode made infinite wydowes ſhoulde recompence theſe domages receyued great triumph haſt thou ſene greter foly infinite nombre diſtroyed warre one alone ſhal beare away glorie therof though ſuche miſerable conquerours merited buried yet whan went ſtretes rome telle ſecrete betwene whanne charyotte tryumphaunt came vnhappy pryſoners charged yrons remembring infinite treaſures yll gotten heryng lamentation wydowes ſorowfully wepynge dethe huſbandes callynge mynde manyfolde frendes deed though reioyced openly wepte droppes bloode ſecretely canne telle perſonne taketh pleaſure hym ſelfe mannes dammage caſe prayſe aſſyriens enuye perſians contente lacedemoniens approue caldeens content grekes curſe troyans condempne carthage bycauſe great ignomynious ſhame hath ouerthrowen wolde witte reſte perſone haue truſteth euer vpon proſperitie fortune ſyth ſo lyght cauſe haue ſene ſo great ſtryfe rome ſuche loſſe thy howſe seynge ſee wyll day wold diſcouer ſhuld haue ben crueltie hath ben trouble ſo long ſpace abſence ſhulde haue gyuen knowlege deth ſuche entierly deſired huſbande ben reſon ſhe haue receyued ſo many good dedis ſhuld haue ſo yll newes ſyth houre yt knewe ye wyſte therof peyne hath ben double fele dethe nowe fele deathe ſolytarines thy deſolation thou haſte reaſon wepe goddis reſte v myſerable perſons lyuinge power ſoo many ylles therfore ſhulde ceſſe take peyne ſorowe labinia oftentymes haue thoughte thynge myght fyrſte wepe yll lyuethe good dieth moche hurteth yll found good loſte great peyne ſee theſe innocentes dye ſurely leſſe peyne ſee malicious people lyue neceſſitie muſte nedes come whan cometh ought ſclaundre hit shewe labinia doſte thou knowe howe good conuerſation goddes hope go howe yll men conuerſaunt yll borne dye lyke wyſe good dyethe lyue good man alway lyueth dyenge yll alwayes dyeth lyuynge ſith goddis haue cauſed come theym noo greatte thyng haue taken fro certayne thy deſyred huſban claudyn true frende ſeing remembrynge hath ſcaped rather ſtylle returne agayn trouth remedyes widowes thynke company paſſed ſolytarines preſent thynke reſt hope come hither vnto thou haſt ben peine abidinge thy houſe nowe reioyce bycauſe abideth thou ſhalt moche better entreated amonge goddis amonge men conſent thynke thou haſte loſte hym onely ſyth reioyced lyfe bounde wepe dethe greatteſte ſorowe ſycke harte amonge ſorowes▪ ſe reioyce dolour contrarye wyſe greatteſt eaſe amonge greues fortune ſee feeleth ſorowe frende wepeth eies al feeleth ſorowe diſchargeth ſomewhat myne inwarde peyne bokes tyme auguſte emperour ſheweth howe nere ryuer danubius founde maner people hauynge cuſtome ſame houre whan huſbande taketh wyfe louer wold ſwere goddis neuer wepe ſorowe maner infortune forget theyr owne propre trouble dye remedye theyr louer ſo lykewiſe eche glorious worlde right happy age people eternall memorie wherin men ſo humble louers ſoo true wolde forgette owne ſorowe wepe others rome beinge rome tyme yll ſpente lyfe ylle applied ſmall thoughte recheleſſe theſe dayes harte preſente ſeperate frome welthe aſſured withoute remedy euyll men forgettynge menne tourne ſelfe beaſtes deſire gyue lyfe thou dyeſt take awaye lyfe thou wepeſt ſee laugh laugh ſe wepe thus without profite v leſe reioyce leſynge ſelfe lawe honeſt man ſwere labynia yf thy remedy lay handes thy ſorowe dothe harte thy pytiefulle wepynges ſhoulde hurte thy heuy wofull ſolitarynes thy huſbande ſyth thy remedy deſyre accomplyſſhed deathe deed haue power remyt handes goddis moche ſelfe frend tyme paſt taken ſuſpecte ennemye tyme come thou haſt reputed hytherto thy neyghbour parent thy huſbande praye nowe take thy huſbande loue thy father counſayle ſonne ſeruyce aduocate senate counſell meane remedy claudyne nowe deed frende marc alyue alſo thy deſeruynge thou mayſte commaunde thou wylte loue haue thou mayſte deſyre thynge nedefull pray eſchewe extremitie romayne wydowes al extremity lyeth vyce al ſuche werieth ſelfe anoyeth goddis leſe aliue profit deed gyue ſuſpection yt yl dyd fuluia wife noble marc mercello ſhe ſeing huſbande buried felde mar ſcratched vyſage tare heer brake tethe euery pace ſwowned two ſenatours held armes bycauſe ſhe ſhuld hurt ſelf thā ſaid flauiꝰ cenſurius let alone day ſhe wyl folow iourney widowes ſo while yt bone marcello brennyng ſhe intreting mary huſbād yet noted one ſenatours yt led gaue hande one romain perpetual mariage caſe ſo foule takē euery mā great vilany romains preſent abaſhed ſuſpect neuer beleue wydowe rome ſay labinia bycauſe thou wylt ſo god mar ſwere hart marc hath ſuch ſuſpect thy great age wyll ſuffre auctoritie ſoo ſadde matrone wyll demande require ryght hartily forgette nat honeſtie ought romayn woman retrayte requiſite wydowe yf thou wydowe ſolytarines thou feleſt hym deed comfort reputation holden lyuing wyl ſay tyme thy renome may ſuche men caſt ſuche brydel vpon yll cauſe ſtil theym good gyue theym ſpurres ſerue ye wyll thus take thought beſines ye haue ſenate wyfe fauſtyn greteth oftentymes wepeth myſaduenture ſend money pay thy creditours goddis haue gyuen reſte claudine thy huſbande gyue comforte conſolation labinia wyfe marc mounte celio hath writen owne hande ¶a letter ſent marc themperour cyncinatus frend bycauſe beinge gentylman became marchant vii letter marc edilis cenſure cincinatus capue ſende ſalutation thy perſon force vertue ayenſt ſiniſter fortune syth feaſt bereſcinte mother goddis haue ſene ſeruaunte thy houſe letter thy hand haue redde whiche putteth great ſuſpection thy helthe thou arte ſome peryll el thou diſprayſeſt amitie dyſchargynge thy ſelfe ſoo lyttell thoughte forgette v ſo great recheleſnes thy trauaille ſoo moche writinge ſhuld conſolation rede thy letter thy hande waxe ſtowe frome trauaylle writynge yet enforce myn harte myn eaſe wherin ſemblaunt true frendes wyll put fro annoyaunce thou pleaſure thou knoweſt wel ſmal diſtaunce betwene capue mount celio cauſe frendeſhyppe ſpace hen illirico ſhuld cauſe v ſtraungers delycate wynes ſent theyr owne countrey ſtraungers take greatter myght ferther perſons true frendes ſeperate ſooner oughte vnyte ioyne together myndes shewe pray ye cyncinate ſyth thou haſt euer founde true haſte thou ſuſpecte deſyre grene leu outwarde ſhewethe tree drye inwarde good werkes openly notifieth inward hart ſecretly perfite always breakyng faylyng ſeruice perfytly loueth perpetually faythfully ſerueth moche aſtonied thy ſlouthe demaundynge ſomwhat thy couwardyſe write wyl confeſſe one trouthe thou haddeſte moche hardynes wyll thought ſmalle effecte letter myght ſatiſfie greatenes thyne vnderſtandynge ſhulde abyde yll done ſhorte throweth ſpeare tyme paſte whan yonge thou old thou thy counſayles wich money eche gaue houre thy heed whyte men reken olde yet thy workes accuſe yonge reaſon ſuccour thy pouertie money remedy thy lyghtenes councel good wyll haue lawe amitie owe wyll aduertiſe vertuous man ought remembre benefites hath receyued forget iniuries doone hym eſteme moche owne ſmalle power holde greatnes nothyng fauour good diſſimule euyll great greatteſt communicable inferiours preſentlye doo good dedes alſo abſent ſpeake good wordes greuous loſſes fortune holde theym ſmall eſtemation ſmal loſſe honour holde great eſtemation one thynge aduenture money dyuers doubtfull aduenture certaintie finally frende one ennemie none theſe thinges ought haue amonge good wyll accompted good knowe well thou haſt lefte pretour warre nowe thou haſte ſette thy ſelfe lande ſee vſe marchandyſe thou makeſt ſore abaſhed conquere thyn enmies romayn nowe take office perſecute thy frendes tyrant wylte thou yll thy neyghbours leaue ſtraungers wylt thou take away liuynge fro hym gyueth v liuing take away deth fro taketh away lyfe wilt thou mouers ſtrangers giue moderation fro ſobre take away reſt thou wylt gyue take awaye fro v take fro gyue v delyuer condemned condempne innocentes thou wylt tyraunt common welth defender thy countreye ſithe aduentureth hym leaueth dedes armes becometh marchaunte ſtudye ſoore hath meued leaue chiualrye wherin thou haſte great honour nowe take offyce wherby foloweth ſo moche ſhame rebuke surely thynke none excuſe thou art olde canſt clymbe mountaynes nowe thou ſytteſt ſtylle robbeſt playnes olde men olde malady whan outwarde force fayleth theym forthwith arme malyce inwarde ſaye ſoore couetous perſons thou act one thynge wyll ſay thou haſte taken office wherby thy felowes haue robbed dyuers day thou ſhalt gyue accompte therof one howre ye tyme ſhall come thou ſhalt leſe moment goddis permyt one ſhall chaſtyſement dyuers longe tyme chaſtyſeth howe frende cyncinate howſe thy father cyncinate ſpeares writynges hangynge haue ſene halle full armure fardel portall gate ful knightes marchantis certaynly haue ſene ſcole noblenes denne theues cincinate curſed ſo vilayn office marchātis lyue porely dye ryche let v ſay ageyn curſed bycauſe couetyſe one yll wold accompliſhed preiudice many good wyll hurte thy predeceſſours wyl aduertiſe thy miſerie thy ſucceſſours thou thynkeſt yt thy vertue ſhulde holde ende worlde worlde holdeth hit ſemeth thy white heares holde excuſed trauayle perſwadynge reſon gate ſo great cauſe knocked hāmer ſom warnyng bring good reſon neceſſitie muſt paſſe myll make clere vnderſtandyng tyme tyme nede requireth counſell dyuers time wiſe men fayle bycauſe wold faile thinges ſuche qualitie wyſedom ſuffiſeth aſſure nedefull wyll vntyed vnderſtandyng diſſolued owne propre gold though benchers kynges continue thouſand yere rule entrayles erthe yet fynde ſtedfaſte rocke mountayne wherin clooſe goodes predeceſſours eſtates perpetuall goddis immortall haue made thinges communicable men mortall excepte immortalitie therfore called immortall bicauſe neuer dye called mortall faylyng bycauſe al take ende howe ſtronge ſo euer walles yet great age cauſeth fall ruine two thinges ſemeth free whiche fortune ſet abacke tyme cauſe forgotten theſe good yll renoume amonge men peyne rewarde good yll haue goddis frende cyncinate thus acheueth perſones goddis neuer grene rype rotten holdeth ſeaſon fruyte tree floured eſteme nothynge bycauſe muſte die nature howe dyuers tymes leaues flower beare froſte ſome malady blaſte ſome enuious myſhap longe webbe makyng made many day cut aſonder moment semblably piteous thing ſee man dye ſo great trauayle ſette ſtate honour afterwarde regardynge neyther one yet ſe periſh without memory thing abydynge frende cyncinate loue betwene v pray immortal goddis coniure beleue worlde whiche vnder colour lyttell golde hydeth moche fylthyneſſe vnder colour trouthe chaungeth v lye ſhort delyte gyueth v diſpleaſures ſheweth moſte loue begyleth greatteſt tromperies worlde gyueth moſte goodes procureth moſt domages ſerueth mockery hit rewardeth true recompences loue truly gyueth goodes mockery finally whan ſlepe mooſte ſureſt waketh experience haue knowen fewe howſes paynted ſtalles raiſed vp haue ſene rome ſmall tyme take thoughte walles haue cruelle enmity theyr neyghbours great anoy heyres importunate ſhame frendes double ye ſe make funerall wepynges waylynges dyd deth ſonne yet thynke doth brenne hart ſo inwarde greatte heate conſumed humyditie eies outwarde brennethe ſpyrites inwarde thou mayſte knowe honourable childrē ſerue vyces paſtyme laſt according merites goddis wyll heire heritage ſhulde peryſhe marke ſay hadde two ſonnes comode prince veriſſimus yonger dead greateſt vertue alway imagined good lyued late ſo therwith fortune doth arme apparel v wherin ſhe ſeeth ſhal fal greatteſt hurt therfore goddis permit couetous faders gaderyng great trauayle ſhuld die hurt leue rich vicious childrē yll deed good alway meriteth haue deth bewailed ſay frend catulus thought haue loſt wit whā ſaw ſon veriſſime dye toke comfort ayen either muſt ſe ende cōſidering goddis dyd lend gaue inheriters haue ye incō uenientes done v men offēce commytte ageynſt goddis like caſe honourable honour reſtethe dygnyties haue good workes wherby meryte therby wordes ſeme trewe xi emperour rome bare writen rynge fynger whiche ſayde thus honoured deſerueth honour hath deſerueth theſe wordes greatly noted ſpoken great lorde retourne purpoſe thou complayneſt wronges greues men men leue goddis haue meruayle goddis neuer vniuſte thynges ſo menne neuer lyghtly thynge iuſte note ſay forgette ſenate gyueth open peyne publyſſheth ſecrete faulte ſuche maner peyne hurte v faute ſhame v goddes pitiefull though gyue v pein yet kepe faut cloſe frende antigone though goddes gather togider ſlouthe wyckednes commytte ſecretelye beleue doubte goddis gyue lyfe many whiche men bereueth therfore thynke thou ſhuldeſt thynke wyſhe ſyth goddis haue ſuffred ylles thou haſt done ſecretly thou muſt ſuffre open chaſtyſement men haue gyuen otherwiſe thinkynge put away peyne thou ſhalt abyde charged infamy haue written lōg epyſtle thentent thou ſhuldeſt haue ſome thyng paſſe tyme certaynly greatteſt eaſemente eaſe hym trauayle exercyſe wauerynge harte ſome good occupation wyll write tyme touchynge thy banyſhemente truſte ſhal brynge one ſenate ſende panutius ſecretarie gyue moche credence wordes letter bryngeth gowne therwith harte wylle comforte salutation peace good age theire goddis yll fortune ſeperate fro marke houſehold wyfe chyldrē ſalute thyn ſalute thy family owne thoughe halfe letter hande comforte harte entirely thyne thou knoweſte howe greuouſly hurte warres dacye hande moyſte wether one therfore wyll ſay ſome thinge fynde conſolation thou haſte nede therof lawe rhodes haue founde theſe wordes commaunde none ſo hardy gyue counſail remedy wordes hym yt trouble gyuethe ſmall conſolation whā remedy alſo herte ſorow hath reſt ſhewing greues herynge conſolation thou ſayeſt thy letter cenſures right rigorous realme therfore al nation hath yll wyll ſenate beleue well haue good occaſion therof diſhonoured men make miniſters iuſtice rigorous namely yle ancient prouerbe ſayth lyghtly theſe ylles ar yll siciliens worſt adays yll mighty ylnes good vertues kepte ſo cloſe yf ſome bridell aſhamed cruel ſentence cenſures romayns cruell tyrantes one thyng ſore abaſhed greatly troubleth wyttes ſeinge naturally right iuſtyce goddis good offendyng haue iuſtice lent v yet glorifie v cruell
